name="compile"

description="compile

the

source">


<mkdir

dir="${bin}"/>

groovy

srcdir="src"

destdir="${bin}"

memoryMaximumSize="256m"

failonerror="true"

fork="true"

>


<classpath

refid="classpath"/>


<javac

source="1.6"

target="1.6"

debug="on"/>


</groovyc>


<copy

todir="${bin}">


<fileset

dir="src"

includes="**/*"/>


</copy>
</target>

ThreadLocal

is

apart

If

How

which

to

client

and

and

the

How

to

make

HTTP

Server

in

Java

First

to

is

to

which

can

accept

connection

on

certain

TCP

port

HTTP

server

usually

listen

on

port

80

but

we

will

different

port

8080

for

purpose

You

can

ServerSocket

class

in

to

Server

which

can

requests

as

shown

below

import

){

}

}

on

If

established

and

compile

If

So

but

All

Do

Any

our

and

In

final

Socket

client

server.accept()

This

As

Once

and

So

basically

our

should

import

java.net.ServerSocket;


import

java.net.Socket;


public

class

{

void

Exception

{


final

ServerSocket

server

new

ServerSocket(

8080

);

"Listening

on

port

8080

...."

);


while

true

{


final

Socket

client

server

.accept();


//

1

Read

HTTP

from

the

client

socket

//

2

Prepare

an

HTTP

response

//

3

Send

HTTP

response

to

the

client

//

4

Close

the

socket

}


}
}

This

Server

its

How

to

convert

java.util.Date

to

java.sql.Timestamp?

You

can

convert

java.util.Date

to

java.sql.Timestamp

value

by

using

the

getTime()

method

of

Date

class

This

method

return

the

long

millisecond

value

from

Epoch

(1st

January

1970

midnight)

which

you

can

pass

to

java.sql.Timestamp

to

create

new

instance

of

Timestamp

object

in

JDBC

Remember

java.sql.TimeStamp

†class

is

wrapper

around

java.util.Date

to

allow

JDBC

to

view

it

as

SQL

TIMESTAMP

value

Only

way

to

create

Timestamp

instance

is

by

passing

the

long

time

value

because

the

second

constructor

of

Timestamp

class

which

accepts

individual

fields

e.g

year

month

date

hour

minute

second

and

nano

is

deprecated

Timestamp

class

can

also

hold

up-to

nano

second

value.†

Difference

between

Thread

and

an

Executor

in

Java

Even

Thread

and

Executor

both

are

used

to

executed

some

code

in

parallel

there

are

some

key

differences

between

them.The

main

difference

between

Thread

and

an

Executor

in

Java

is

that

later

provides

thread

pool

in

Java

Along

with

several

concurrency

utilities

like

CountDownLatch

CyclicBarrier

Semaphore

FutureTask

Callable

interface

and

Conditions

JDK

also

introduced

built-in

thread

pool

which

provides

set

of

working

threads

to

run

your

code

in

parallel

Since

creating

starting

and

running

thread

is

time-consuming

and

expensive

operation

many

Java

applications

create

pool

of

thread

at

start-up

and

leverage

that

for

executing

the

task

in

parallel

until

Java

introduced

the

built-in

thread

pool

†This

thread-pool

is

known

as

Executor

framework

which

relieved

Java

application

developers

from

the

responsibility

of

creating

and

managing

threads

more

Difference

between

Executor

Framework

and

ForkJoinPool

in

Java?

Java

added

Executor

Framework

to

provide

out-of-box

thread

pool

to

Java

programmers

and

Java

added

ForkJoinPool

an

implementation

of

ExecutorService

which

specifically

designed

to

execute

ForkJoinTask

The

Executor

Framework

provides

several

classes

e.g

Executor

ExecutorService

and

Executors

for

execution

and

creating

thread

pools

It

also

provides

several

built-in

ready

to

use

thread

pools

like

pool

of

fixed

threads

cached

thread

pool

which

can

expand

itself

spawn

new

threads

if

required

due

to

heavy

load

How

You

This

long

millisecond

from

Epoch

(1st

to

java.sql.Timestamp

Remember

java.sql.TimeStamp

Date

ZipFile

ZIP

in

world

Zip

file

may

contains

multiples

files

or

folder

in

compressed

format

†Java

API

provides

extensive

support

to

read

Zip

files

all

related

to

zip

file

are

located

in

java.util.zip

package

One

of

the

†most

common

task

related

to

zip

archive

is

to

read

and

display

what

entries

it

then

extract

them

folder

In

will

to

do

this

task

in

Java

There

are

two

ways

you

can

iterate

over

all

items

in

given

zip

archive

you

can

use

either†

java.util.zip.ZipFile

or

java.util.zip.ZipInputStream

Since

Zip

file

contains

several

items

each

of

them

has

header

field

containing

size

of

items

in

number

of

bytes

Which

means

you

can

iterate

all

entries

without

actually

decompressing

the

zip

file

Difference

between

Inheritance

and

Composition

in

Java

OOPS

Though

both

Inheritance

and

Composition

provide

code

reusablility

main

difference

between

Composition

and

Inheritance

in

Java

is

that

Composition

allows

reuse

of

code

without

extending

it

but

for

Inheritance

you

must

extend

the

class

for

any

reuse

of

code

or

functionality

Another

difference

which

comes

from

this

fact

is

that

by

using

Composition

you

can

reuse

code

for

even

final

class

which

is

not

extensible

but

Inheritance

cannot

reuse

code

in

such

cases

Also

by

using

Composition

you

can

reuse

code

from

many

classes

as

they

are

declared

as

just

member

variable

but

with

Inheritance

you

can

reuse

code

form

just

one

class

because

in

Java

you

can

only

extend

one

class

because

multiple

Inheritance

is

not

supported

in

Java

Read

more
